<p>The <b>Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank</b> (<b>AIIB</b>) is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_financial_institution" title="International financial institution">international financial institution</a> that aims to support the building of infrastructure in the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a> region. The bank has 50 member states (all "Founding Members") and was proposed as an initiative by the government of China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The initiative gained support from 37 regional and 20 non-regional Prospective Founding Members (PFM), all of which have signed the Articles of Agreement that form the legal basis for the bank. The bank started operation after the agreement entered into force on 25 December 2015, after ratifications were received from 10 member states holding a total number of 50% of the initial subscriptions of the Authorized Capital Stock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOAtext_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-AOAtext-5">[5]</a></sup> Major economies that did not become PFM include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven_(G7)" title="Group of Seven (G7)">G7</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Eight_(G8)" title="Group of Eight (G8)">G8</a> members' <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, although Canada applied for membership on 23 September 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United Nations has addressed the launch of AIIB as having potential for "scaling up financing for sustainable development"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> for the concern of global economic governance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The capital of the bank is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Dollar" title="US Dollar">$</a>100 billion, equivalent to <span class="nowrap"> </span><span class="frac nowrap"><sup>2</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> of the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> and about half that of the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The bank was proposed by China in 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and the initiative was launched at a ceremony in Beijing in October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The proposal for the creation of an "Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank" was first made by the Vice Chairman of the China Center for International Economic Exchanges, a Chinese thinktank, at the Bo'ao Forum in April 2009. The initial context was to make better use of Chinese foreign currency reserves in the wake of the global financial crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The initiative was officially launched by Chinese President Xi Jinping on a state visit to Indonesia in October 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The Chinese government has been frustrated with what it regards as the slow pace of reforms and governance, and wants greater input in global established institutions like the IMF, World Bank and Asian Development Bank which it claims are dominated by American, European and Japanese interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lowyinterpreter2014_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-lowyinterpreter2014-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014, Chinese Premier <a href="/wiki/Li_Keqiang" title="Li Keqiang">Li Keqiang</a> delivered a keynote speech at the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Boao_Forum_for_Asia" title="Boao Forum for Asia">Boao Forum for Asia</a> and said that China was ready to intensify consultations with relevant parties in and outside Asia on the preparations for the Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank_Institute" title="Asian Development Bank Institute">Asian Development Bank Institute</a> published a report in 2010 which said that the region requires $8 trillion to be invested from 2010 to 2020 in infrastructure for the region to continue economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lowyinterpreter2014_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-lowyinterpreter2014-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In a 2014 editorial, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> newspaper wrote that the new bank could allow Chinese capital to finance these projects and allow it a greater role to play in the economic development of the region commensurate with its growing economic and political clout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> But until March 2015, China in the ADB has only 5.47 percent voting right, while Japan and US have a combined 26 percent voting right (13 percent each) with a share in subscribed capital of 15.7 percent and 15.6 percent, respectively. Dominance by both countries and slow reforms underlie China's wish to establish the AIIB, while both countries worry about China's increasing influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014 China proposed doubling the registered capital of the bank from $50 billion to $100 billion and invited India to participate in the founding of the bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> On 24 October 2014, twenty-one countries signed a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) regarding the AIIB in Beijing, China: Bangladesh, Brunei, Cambodia, India, Kazakhstan, Kuwait, Laos, Malaysia, Myanmar, Mongolia, Nepal, Oman, Pakistan, Philippines, Qatar, Singapore, Sri Lanka, Thailand, Uzbekistan and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Indonesia's joining was slightly delayed due to their new presidential administration not being able to review the membership in time. Indonesia signed the MOU on 25 November 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indonesia_membership_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-indonesia_membership-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The U.S. allegedly tried to keep Australia and South Korea from becoming prospective founding members, after they expressed an interest in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> However, both Australia and South Korea applied to join the bank in March 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hong Kong's <a href="/wiki/Financial_Secretary_(Hong_Kong)" title="Financial Secretary (Hong Kong)">Financial Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Tsang" title="John Tsang">John Tsang</a> announced in his budget speech in February 2015 that the territory would join the AIIB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> It did however not become one of the prospective founding members and negotiated as part of the Chinese delegation.</p>
<p>In early March 2015, the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Osborne" title="George Osborne">George Osborne</a>, announced that the UK had decided to apply to join the Bank, becoming the first major Western country to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The announcement was criticised by the U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obama_Administration" title="Obama Administration">Obama Administration</a>. A US government official told <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i>, "We are wary about a trend toward constant accommodation of China, which is not the best way to engage a rising power." The official further stated that the British decision was taken after "no consultation with the US."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In response, the UK indicated that the subject had been discussed between Chancellor Osborne and US Treasury Secretary <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lew" title="Jack Lew">Jack Lew</a> for several months preceding the decision. It was further stated that joining the bank as a founding member would allow the UK to influence the development of the institution. By encouraging Chinese investments in the next generations of nuclear power plants, Osborne announced that "the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> would become the base for the first clearing house for the yuan outside Asia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the criticism, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council" title="United States National Security Council">White House National Security Council</a>, in a statement to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, declared,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Our position on the AIIB remains clear and consistent. The United States and many major global economies all agree there is a pressing need to enhance infrastructure investment around the world. We believe any new multilateral institution should incorporate the high standards of the World Bank and the regional development banks. Based on many discussions, we have concerns about whether the AIIB will meet these high standards, particularly related to governance, and environmental and social safeguards […] The international community has a stake in seeing the AIIB complement the existing architecture, and to work effectively alongside the World Bank and Asian Development Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Several other European states – including Germany, France and Italy – followed the UK's decision to join the AIIB in March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> German Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Sch%C3%A4uble" title="Wolfgang Schäuble">Wolfgang Schäuble</a> stated, "We want to contribute our long-standing experience with international financial institutions to the creation of the new bank by setting high standards and helping the bank to get a high international reputation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In March 2015, the South Korean Ministry of Strategy and Finance announced that it, too, is planning to join the AIIB, citing its potential in helping South Korean companies win deals in infrastructural projects as well expanding South Korea's influence in international banking as a founding member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> States could indicate their interest in becoming a Prospective Founding Member until 31 March 2015.</p>
<p>Negotiations took place in the framework of five Chief Negotiators Meetings (CNMs) which took place between November 2014 and May 2015. The Articles of Agreement, the legal framework of the bank, were concluded in the fifth CNM. It was signed on 29 June 2015 by 50 of the named 57 prospective founding members in Beijing, while the other seven signed later.</p>
<p>On 25 December 2015, the Articles of Agreement entered into force. On 16 January 2016, the board of governors of the bank convened its inaugural meeting in Beijing and declared the bank open for business. <a href="/wiki/Jin_Liqun" title="Jin Liqun">Jin Liqun</a> was elected as the bank's president for a five-year term. 17 states (Australia, Austria, Brunei, China, Georgia, Germany, Jordan, Luxembourg, Mongolia, Myanmar, the Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Pakistan, Singapore, South Korea and the United Kingdom) together holding 50.1% of the initial subscriptions of Authorized Capital Stock, had deposited the instrument of ratification for the agreement, triggering entry into force, and making them all founding members<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treatybase_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-treatybase-35">[35]</a></sup> and bringing the Articles of Agreement, the bank's charter, into force. 12 other states followed later, taking the amount of Authorized Capital Stock held by the 29 members of the bank to 74%.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AIIB_within_PRC_policy_thinking">AIIB within PRC policy thinking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: AIIB within PRC policy thinking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fostering_long-term_economic_development">Fostering long-term economic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fostering long-term economic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank can be construed as a natural inter-national extension of the <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure-based_development" title="Infrastructure-based development">infrastructure-driven economic development</a> framework that has sustained the rapid economic growth of China since the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_reform" title="Chinese economic reform">Chinese economic reform</a> under chairman <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a>. It stems from the notion that long-term economic growth can only be achieved through massive, systematic, and broad-based investments in infrastructure assets – in contrast with the more short-term "export-driven" and "domestic consumption" development models favored by mainstream <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoclassical_economists" title="Neoclassical economists">Neoclassical economists</a> and pursued inconsiderately by many developing countries in the 1990s and the first decade of the 21st century with generally disappointing results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euromoney_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Euromoney-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAK-JTW_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAK-JTW-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_as_regional_integration_and_foreign_policy_tool">Infrastructure as regional integration and foreign policy tool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Infrastructure as regional integration and foreign policy tool">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In his 29 March 2015 speech at the <a href="/wiki/Boao_Forum_for_Asia" title="Boao Forum for Asia">Boao Forum for Asia</a> (BFA) annual conference, President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> said:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>[T]he Chinese economy is deeply integrated with the global economy and forms an important driving force of the economy of Asia and even the world at large. […] China's investment opportunities are expanding. Investment opportunities in infrastructure connectivity as well as in new technologies, new products, new business patterns, and new business models are constantly springing up. […] China's foreign cooperation opportunities are expanding. We support the multilateral trading system, devote ourselves to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doha_Round" title="Doha Round">Doha Round</a> negotiations, advocate the Asia-Pacific free trade zone, promote negotiations on regional comprehensive economic partnership, advocate the construction of the Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB), boost economic and financial cooperation in an all-round manner, and work as an active promoter of <a href="/wiki/Economic_globalization" title="Economic globalization">economic globalization</a> and regional integration</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Xi insisted also that the Silk Road Fund and the Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank would foster "economic connectivity and a new-type of industrialization [in the Asia Pacific area], and [thus] promote the common development of all countries as well as the peoples' joint enjoyment of development fruits."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRC_MFA_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRC_MFA-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_basis_and_membership">Legal basis and membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Legal basis and membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em">

<th scope="row">Languages</th>

</table>
<p>The Articles of Agreement form the legal basis for the Bank. 57 Prospective Founding Members (PFM) named in annex A of the agreement are eligible to sign and ratify the Articles, thus becoming a member of the Bank. Other states, which are parties to the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> may become members after approval of their accession by the bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOAtext_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-AOAtext-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Articles were negotiated by the Prospective Founding Members, with Hong Kong joining the negotiations via China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HK_blog_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-HK_blog-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_members">Founding members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Founding members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 57 Prospective Founding Members can become Founding Members through:</p>
<ul>
<li>Signing the Articles of Agreement in 2015</li>
<li>Ratifying the Articles of Agreement in 2015 or 2016</li>
</ul>
<p>All Prospective Founding Members have signed the Articles, 49 of which have ratified them, comprising 91.81% of the shares of all PFM. The formal actions towards becoming a Founding Member are shown below, as well as the percentage of the votes and of the shares, in the event all prospective founding states become parties, and no other members are accepted.</p>

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CDF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Regional members</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non_prospective_founding_members">Non prospective founding members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Non prospective founding members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Of the states without Prospective Founding Member status, Belgium, Canada, Czech Republic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Hungary, Taiwan and Ukraine are considering joining the AIIB as members. Colombia, Japan and the United States have no immediate intention to participate. Taiwan's request to become a Prospective Founding Member was rejected by China as it does not consider the former to be a sovereign state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taiwan_rejected_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-taiwan_rejected-67">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dependent_territories">Dependent territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dependent territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Articles of Agreement provide for non-sovereign entities to become members of the bank. In addition to the requirements for sovereign states, the membership of dependent territories must be supported by the state responsible for its external relations.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/45px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Hong Kong – Hong Kong SAR's representative attended the third Chief Negotiators' Meeting (CNM) held for Prospective Founding Members (PFM) on 30–31 March 2015 by joining the delegation of China,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> and what kind of form or identity that Hong Kong SAR will be in AIIB will be finally determined once the preparing procedure or the negotiation is completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HK_Membership_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-HK_Membership-69">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Chinese_Taipei_for_Olympic_games.svg/23px-Flag_of_Chinese_Taipei_for_Olympic_games.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Chinese_Taipei_for_Olympic_games.svg/35px-Flag_of_Chinese_Taipei_for_Olympic_games.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Chinese_Taipei_for_Olympic_games.svg/45px-Flag_of_Chinese_Taipei_for_Olympic_games.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span>Chinese Taipei (Taiwan) – Taiwan applied for PFM to join the AIIB via <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Affairs_Office" title="Taiwan Affairs Office">Taiwan Affairs Office</a> on 31 March, possibly under the name "Chinese Taipei",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> but was rejected by the Multilateral Interim Secretariat of the AIIB on 13 April, without any reason stated. However, China claims that there is the possibility for Taiwan to obtain membership at a later date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taiwan_rejected_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-taiwan_rejected-67">[65]</a></sup> China's Foreign Ministry spokeswoman <a href="/wiki/Hua_Chunying" title="Hua Chunying">Hua Chunying</a> said that Taiwan should avoid creating a "two Chinas" or "one China, one Taiwan" situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Taiwan)" title="Ministry of Finance (Taiwan)">ROC Finance Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Chang_Sheng-ford" title="Chang Sheng-ford">Chang Sheng-ford</a> announced in April 2016 that Taiwan was not being treated with "dignity" or "respect" during the registration process and Taiwan eventually chose to leave the decision to join to the new president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_states">Other states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> United States – <b>No commitment</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The United States' officials have expressed concerns about whether the AIIB would have high standards of governance, and whether it would have environmental and social safeguards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-74">[72]</a></sup> The United States is reported to have used diplomatic pressure to try and prevent key allies, such as Australia, from joining the bank,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> and expressed disappointment when others, such as Britain, joined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-econ_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-econ-62">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-74">[72]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan"><img alt="Japan" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> Japan – <b>"Under Consideration" / No commitment</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Masato_Kitera" title="Masato Kitera">Masato Kitera</a>, Tokyo's envoy in Beijing, stated previously that Japan might join the AIIB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> Japanese Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Tar%C5%8D_As%C5%8D" title="Tarō Asō">Tarō Asō</a> previously indicated interest in joining the AIIB, but later switched his stance. <a href="/wiki/Yoshihide_Suga" title="Yoshihide Suga">Yoshihide Suga</a>, Japan's Cabinet Secretary, told the public that Japan was still seeking China's full explanation of the AIIB as he stated, "As of today, Japan will not join AIIB and a clear explanation has not been received from China" and "Japan is dubious about whether (the AIIB) would be properly governed or whether it would damage other creditors". He also stated that Japan is no longer considering whether or not to join the bank. The Japanese Government Spokesman also announced that Japan would not join the AIIB. Japanese prime minister <a href="/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe" title="Shinzō Abe">Shinzō Abe</a> also added that Japan does not need to join the bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TJ_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-TJ-77">[75]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shareholding_structure">Shareholding structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Shareholding structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Authorized Capital Stock of the bank is 100 billion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Dollar" title="US Dollar">US Dollars</a>, divided into 1 million shares of 100 000 dollars each. Twenty percent are paid-in shares (and thus have to be transferred to the bank), and 80% are callable shares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoA_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-AoA-2">[2]</a></sup> The allocated shares are based on the size of each member country's economy (calculated using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP" title="List of countries by GDP">GDP Nominal</a> (60%) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP" title="List of countries by real GDP">GDP PPP</a> (40%)), whether they are an Asian or Non-Asian Member, and the number of shares determines the fraction of authorized capital in the bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOAtext_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-AOAtext-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> Of the prospective founding members, three states decided not to subscribe to all allocated shares: Malaysia, Portugal and Singapore,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NLreport_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-NLreport-43">[42]</a></sup> resulting in 98% of available shares to be subscribed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AoA_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-AoA-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three categories of votes exist: basic votes, share votes and Founding Member votes. The basic votes are equal for all members and constitute 12% of the total votes, while the share votes are equal to the number of shares. Each Founding Member furthermore gets 600 votes. An overview of the shares, assuming when all 57 Prospective Founding Members have become Founding Members is shown below (values in bold do not depend on the number of members):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportCH_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-reportCH-42">[41]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The bank's governance structure is composed of the Board of Governors<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> as the top-level and highest decision-making body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-about-82">[80]</a></sup> It is composed of 1 governor for each member state of the bank and in principle meets once a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-about-82">[80]</a></sup> The board of directors, composed of 12 governors, each representing one or more member is responsible for daily operations and tasks delegated to it by the board of governors. Nine of those members are from within the Asia-Pacific region and three representing members outside the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-about-82">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the non-regional directors, 1 constituency is made up of EU member states having the Euro as their currency, and 1 from other European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NLupdate_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-NLupdate-83">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>New members are considered for admission only once a year. An overview of the constituencies is shown below:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The President of the World Bank, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Yong_Kim" title="Jim Yong Kim">Jim Yong Kim</a>, has said that the need for infrastructure in developing countries is great so that the activities of new organizations would be welcome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geopolitical_implication_in_Asia_and_beyond">Geopolitical implication in Asia and beyond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geopolitical implication in Asia and beyond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Think-tanks such as <a href="/wiki/Chatham_House" title="Chatham House">Chatham House</a>, the China Studies Centre at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sydney" title="University of Sydney">University of Sydney</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Pensions_%26_Investments_Forum" title="World Pensions &amp; Investments Forum">World Pensions Council (WPC)</a> have argued that the successful establishment of a new supranational financial powerhouse headquartered in PRC would be facilitated by the fact that “<i>the UK seemingly broke from the G7 pack and announced it would join the AIIB. France, Germany, Italy, Australia, Russia, South Korea and Israel soon followed suit – with only Washington and Tokyo remaining outside the new multilateral bank</i>.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Analyse_Financi.C3.A8re_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Analyse_Financi.C3.A8re-86">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chatham_House_Asia_Programme_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chatham_House_Asia_Programme-87">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>These experts observe that the establishment of the Beijing-based AIIB “<i>needn’t trigger vain geopolitical rivalries. China and the West can work successfully together to build a more prosperous, equitable economic order across the Asia-Paciﬁc region</i>”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Analyse_Financi.C3.A8re_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Analyse_Financi.C3.A8re-86">[84]</a></sup> and that the decision by the UK to “<i>join the China-instigated Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank</i> […] <i>shows overdue strategic clarity, and awareness among the political establishment that foreign policy towards China should aim to advance the national interest rather than placate Britain’s other allies</i>” <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chatham_House_Asia_Programme_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chatham_House_Asia_Programme-87">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the proposed bank has no management or approved loans, it has no environmental record. Several organisations<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2015)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> have however expressed their concerns over environmental policy of the proposed bank because of the high stake of China in the bank's business. Although the proposed bank declared "AIIB will learn from the best practice in the world and adopt international standards of environmental protection," Oxford scholar of economics and energy policy Yuge Ma has argued that this may be complicated in developing Asian countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
